<Text>This winery is absolutely the definition of picturesque! A tiny gem from the 1920s in Sonoma not more than an hour from San Francisco makes this an ideal weekend getaway. They are family owned and operated including the head chef!

Their tasting menu ($60/person) with 4 wines and 3 small plates, all locally sourced, is perfect for family or friends to spend a pleasurable hour or two on their outdoor patio but still an intimate setting unlike other larger crowded wineries in the area. We didn‚Äôt have reservations but they were able to squeeze us in, but you should definitely book in advance. Their Chardonnay really stood out with it‚Äôs crisp flavor. < review>
Absolutely wonderful experience all around. I was visiting with family from Minnesota, and since we happened to be in the area I called the morning of on the off chance they would have an opening and got lucky! They managed to fit us in, but it didn't feel like we were last minute additions! We were greeted warmly and everything was prepared beautifully for us.

The wine was the best I've ever tasted, hands down. The food pairings went perfectly with the wine, and the staff member working with us, Anna I believe, was so helpful and pleasant and clearly in love with what she was doing. We learned a ton about what we were drinking, the history of the area, and the process of wine-making in general. A fascinating conversation.

The setting was spectacular, with rustic picnic tables under beautiful trees on a hillside overlooking the valley, with a view of the water and the stunning hills. It was like a fairytale and I could have easily stayed all day. We couldn't have asked for a more perfect experience, and it was undoubtedly a highlight of our trip.< /review>

Scribe Winery is a cut above and beyond the typical wine tour circuit. There is no tasting room with robotic pours and disinterested explanations but rather a handful of picnic tables scattered on a hillside overlooking the vineyard. Reservations are a must. This is the way all vineyards should be run.<//Text>

< Text>
My experience of Scribe wasn't bad, but it wasn't as stunning as some other reviews may make it out to be. There were great views, and there were delicious snacks with the tasting, but it was $25 for 4 pours ‚Äî three of which were chardonnay. Our server was sweet but not very attentive, and we spent a lot of time between pours waiting. The signage coming in was *terrible* and both we and the friends we met almost wound up at the giant house that's in the middle of the area. The skin-on chardonnay was interesting, but not necessary. The idea of "always experimenting" is okay, but there are established methods of wine making for a reason.

If you're going for a leisurely afternoon in the sun and shade, this is a great place. If you're going for a variety of wines, looking for something to buy, and to experience true Sonoma wines, skip Scribe, where you're paying for the ambiance and experience, not the wine tasting itself.<//Text>

<Text>The view is amazing, but that's about all I can recommend.  Some suggestions for the winery:  please have signage from the street, something other than a spray painted sign on a piece of plywood. < Review>
This winery is simply amazing.  It's fairly new, as far as I know, which means that the wines aren't ridiculously over priced.  Rather than having a tasting room (as of August 2010) they have outdoor tasting on top of a hill overlooking the vineyards and a remarkable view of the south Sonoma Valleys towards the bay.  The pinot noir is amazing, as is their cab. The only regret I have is that they don't have a huge selection just yet, but what they make is worth drinking every drop.  Definitely worth the stop!</Review>

<Rate>4<//Rate>< Text>
Service was great, all 3 people behind the counter were super friendly and attentive. Food is great! Fish tastes super fresh and every add on is also great tasting. The place is clean and organized.

The only downside is for the small portion the price is big. We got two small bowls which are around half of what you would get at any other poke place and it ended up being $28 with no drinks or anything, so heads up if you're on a budget.

Other than that, great poke place!< /Text>

Identified potential replacement of an older crown that wasn't done properly. Went back few weeks later to do routine teeth cleaning, and the nightmare started. She performed a wishy washy cleaning, said I had some gum cleaning, asked me to come back in 2 weeks to perform a new periodontal chart, so I did. She started to poke very hard into my gum pockets, and produced numbers almost double what their dentist identified couple months prior. She said I have to do a deep cleaning and apply antibiotics to 21 teeth! Cost is a whopping $3700. I laughed and said no way. Went back to my old dentist 3 weeks later for routine cleaning, they found hardly any bleeding and the periodontal chart depths were almost exactly as what the dentist produced at Bright Dental.  I knew the hygienist was a scam. Last month called them to do a routine teeth cleaning (been 6 months), and they replied that they will only do a deep cleaning. Told them I am not interested, and they insisted. SO I went back for another periodontal chart evaluation, and the same hygienist (Harpeet) , showed her numbers and the numbers from my other dentist office, she got defensive , told me if you don't trust us then why come here. Explained to her that I was giving this office a chance to earn my business and find out how could the periodontal chart numbers vary so drastically in less than 3 weeks. She proceeded to redo the chart and this time she was inserting the probe even harder (remember this is inserting a metal probe into gum tissue, insert until you feel resistance, not keep inserting into soft tissue to get extra depth readings). Anyway, she said the numbers are still too deep and she would only do deep cleaning. I requested the dentist, Dr. Wendell came and said ethically they cant perform regular cleaning, told him that I would sign him a waver, do a regular cleaning, he said he trusts the hygienist numbers, even though his own numbers were less by 2-3 mms per reading. He retorted that different operators can get different numbers by 2-3 mms, so essentially the margin of error is 3 mms, so told him if you subtract 3 mms from her readings, then my depths would all be 3 or less, and thus normal. He still claimed its unethical. I told him that you cant force a particular treatment on a patient , we are not in Cuba, and this is coming across as a scam, want to rip patients off. He gave me the spiel that this is not ethical, and he can only do deep cleaning or nothing. I told him I made a mistake coming to this office. I later called their corporate office and complained, they had the office manager call me, explained to her what happened, she insisted that they won't do regular cleaning, only deep cleaning. Cut a long story short, I switched to another dental office nearby, this practice is a rip off, stay away.</Review>< pics>

< review>
I played here for the first time last weekend and it's now the only place I want to go.  A buddy and I tried to go to Santa Clara but they don't allow outside paint. On a whim, we decided to check this place out, and I'm so glad I did. Cliff is extremely friendly, clearly loves paintball, and goes the extra mile to personally make sure you're having a good time. The fields are unique, with some really fun twists on classic field types. And if you're a bit tired of showing up and only seeing CS2's and Luxe's, this place has insane diversity. Autocockers, pump guns, magfed, old-school guns and just about anything you can imagine was being played. If you're looking for a place that really shows off the best of this sport, there is no place in the bay area I'd recommend more than American. I plan on playing here a few times a month from now on.</review>

<Time>1502217316410</Time><pics>None< /pics>< review>
I visited American Paintball Park a couple of weekends ago for my son's 13th birthday party. Paintball is not an activity I personally would get excited about, so I wasn't thinking I'd care much one way or the other about the experience, much less write a Google review. But Clif and his team, and the experience they create for their guests, are awesome! First off, they have an enthusiasm and sense of fun about the sport that is positively contagious. They are very clear about the safety rules and procedures, and stay on top of safety at all times without being gruff about it. Our group got its own guide out on the play field and he was helpful as both a "referee" and instructor. He never missed a beat, taking them out for a break when they were tired and thirsty and rallying them to get back at it when it was time to head back out for more paintball action. Best of all, they outfitted Granddad with a mask and safety vest so he could go out and get some good video of the kids in action. I also appreciated the easy of booking the party online and the follow up email I received from Clif confirming the reservation. Top notch service from start to finish!<//review>

<Review>I recently moved into the bay area (from TX) and was looking for a place to "call home". American Paintball Park is absolutely, 100%, no questions asked my new "home field". On a Sunday (27 June) I had originally planned on visiting another local field but after seeing the rave reviews I was convinced to spend the extra 20 minutes driving to experience this field. I was thoroughly impressed! I showed up as a solo player wanting to join the public games (and dragging my girlfriend and daughter along to watch as well).

The experience was above par from the moment we pulled into the driveway (speaking of which, Google Maps will give you the incorrect directions, having you enter towards the back of the property,  a trip around the block has you at the right spot). Paintball masks line the fences and as you pull up the owner is standing there to shake your hand, thank you for you coming out and pointing you in the right direction for registration.

Prices were fair, if not below what I've seen available elsewhere in the area. It's clearly a family run operation and I like that, the owner was excellent when it came to making the rounds during breaks, talking with everyone and getting good conversation going between separate parties. When I was out playing a game, then rejoined my family, they were always relaying stories of how the family came over and talked to them, introduced them to their pets (Chicken Dog!) and made them feel more than welcome.

The players at this field are exceptionally nice, assisting with equipment needs (I forgot to bring a rag and a squeegee) and the regular players step in and assist the staff with tasks like air refills. The staff was always on point, calling players out as necessary and emphasizing when an out player was leaving the field. They also chrono before every game which I found to be extremely professional - this field focuses on safety! Masks on early, well before the chrono station and barrel socks on before exiting the field.

There's a nice, unique, selection of fields - although I would rank them on the smaller scale of what I've experienced in the past (coming from a woodsball background). Games are primarily elimination style and the park features a number of different fields focused on various themes (hay bails/rock walls, stool bunkers, door (provided by Google I learned) and dirt mounds. The doors field is a particularly unique design I had never seen before that was a joy to play on. There's also an attack/defend field consisting of an uphill climb for attackers against a small team of defenders within a building facade.

There's a minimal snack bar that's not outrageously expensive (50 cents for a bottle of water) and they grill hot dogs for lunch ($3 gets you a very large hot dog and a bag of chips). Games were run very frequently, with 10-15 minute breaks in-between. I arrived around 10:30, left at 3:00 and played 5 games experiencing every field except for the dirt mounds. There's plenty of shaded seating for observers and break periods and they seemed very accommodating when it came to moving benches/tables around to setup personal grills, birthdays, etc.

I absolutely love this park, probably more so than my "home park" in Texas. They did such a great job at making us feel like part of the family, we were more than welcome there and they were truly appreciative that we would come spend the day with them,

My only cons (and they weren't enough to mark this review down from a 5):
- Some of the fields are close together. I noticed some players engaging players from another field.
- The "out players" area isn't clearly identified on each field and often times in a danger zone between the two games - you may very likely get hit while waiting for the next round.
- The field design is entirely centered around elimination - you won't find any long-form or scenario-type games here.

I've certainly found my new home field. If you see a blonde in a tan flight suit, enjoying every damn moment he spends out here, give me a fist bump.</Review>< pictures>

<Text>This bar. Now, I've never been to this bar, but you don't have to visit to understand that it is a great place in the better part of downtown Fullerton. What sold it for me without the need to even buy a drink is the hospitality of the owner, a kind person with a look of respect for anybody willing to do someone a favor expecting nothing in return and carrying the willingness to offer a helping hand to a complete stranger, with a smile on the side and an obvious passion to keep their business afloat in these trying times. <Text>Recently visited on an early Saturday evening. The atmosphere of this place seems to be more like a bar than a restaurant. We had reservations and had to walk around to find someone to help us check in. Once seated, we noticed that there was a live band, and multiple tvs playing sports. The noise level was moderate to a bit high. Getting back to the food, we shared chili cheese tots, I had the pork chop which comes with creamed corn and potatoes,  while my friend had the Chicken gumbo. We both thought the food here tasted great & glad we made the trip to downtown Fullerton. Service was attentive and friendly.  Parking close by in a lot and structure. Free parking before 9 pm. The cost for the dinner with one iced tea & one premium beer and tax came to just under $60.<//Text>< pictures>

< Text>
Buffalo Chicken ($3.50 each) is topped with bleu cheese coleslaw and served on a grilled sweet Hawaiian roll. It has that vinegary buffalo sauce aroma when it comes to the table so you know it‚Äôs going to be good. It is just spicy enough to get the taste buds going. The coleslaw adds a crunchy texture but could use more bleu cheese. Rating: 4.5/5

Cheeseburger ($3.50 each) is topped with thousand island, tomato, red onion, cheddar cheese, basil aioli, and served on a grilled sweet Hawaiian roll. The beef patty has a flavorful grind and is very juicy. The basil aioli is the kicker. The herbaceous flavor is refreshing and matches perfectly with the beefy slider. Rating: 4.3/5

Beer Battered Alaskan Cod ($3.50 each) is topped with Cajun tartar sauce, coleslaw, and served on a grilled sweet Hawaiian roll. This is definitely the lightest of the slider selections. The cod is crispy on the outside and succulent on the inside. The coleslaw adds a creamy flavor and crunchy texture. Overall, it needs something to punch up the flavor ‚Äì either acidity like vinegar and/or sweetness by adding pineapple into the slaw. Rating: 3.7/5

Fried Mozzarella ($3.50 each) is crusted with panko, topped with sriracha honey jam, basil aioli, and served on a grilled sweet Hawaiian roll. Imagine a baked brie in slider form. The mozzarella has a crispy exterior and creamy, gooey interior. The honey sriracha jam adds a fruity sweetness like a baked brie. The basil aioli adds a touch of herbaceous flavor. Rating: 4.7/5

Fried Chicken ($3.50 each) topped with garlic mashed potatoes, country sausage gravy, and served on a grilled sweet Hawaiian roll. This is my first time having mashed potatoes on a slider and it is great! The mashed potatoes have a creamy texture and perfect garlic flavor. The fried chicken is crispy and seasoned to perfection. The gravy adds a creamy, sausage flavor reminiscent of biscuits and gravy. This slider could use some acidity to really put it over top. A dill pickle would be perfect. Rating: 4.9/5

N‚ÄôAwlins Burger ($3.50 each) is topped with caramelized onions, gorgonzola, garlic aioli, ginger slaw, and served on a grilled sweet Hawaiian roll. The beef patty has a flavorful grind and is very juicy. The first thing that hits you is the sweet caramelized onions. The creamy, tangy gorgonzola balances out the sweetness. The slaw adds a crunchy texture. Rating: 4.9/5

Pulled Pork Slider ($3.50 each) is one of the Sexy Southern Sliders topped with ginger slaw and voodoo BBQ sauce. The pulled pork is ultra-tender and just melts in your mouth. A little salt would pump up the porky flavor. The slaw adds a crunchy texture. Rating: 4/5<//Text>

<rating>5</rating>< review>
One of the most iconic streets in the world, and the center of New Orleans‚Äô party scene, Bourbon Street is located in the Big Easy‚Äôs oldest neighborhood, the French Quarter. The street extends for 13 blocks and is lined with bars, restaurants and souvenir shops.

Bourbon Street Tip:
One easy way to avoid the bulk of the crowds is to stick to visiting during the day, when it‚Äôs relatively quiet (one major exception: during Mardi Gras, when more than 100,000 people swarm the street). The hot and sticky months of June through September are low season, as are December, January and Lent, the seven-week period after the festivities of Mardi Gras.< /review>

<Rate>1<//Rate><Text>I am very saddened to have to write this review but I feel compelled to. The beauty of having Yelp and being a fellow Yelper is being able to share your experience with others.

This morning, Jan 31st 2019, I was getting some grocery shopping done at Cardenas. As I was walking around the store I was taking pictures, you know, for Yelp of course. Then a store employee by the name of Aaron walked up to me and asked me "do you work for another vendor or some other company?". I said "No I do not". Aaron replied "It's because I saw you taking pictures". I told him the pictures were for Yelp. I asked Aaron "if he knew of yelp?" He said he did but it didn't seem genuine.

Aaron advised me that they have a "no video or photography" policy. I explained to Aaron that Yelp is an App where customers leave reviews for businesses and post photos of products. Aaron then said "he would allow the pictures of I left a good review" ü§î. While Aaron wasn't rude by any means, the whole encounter threw me off. I frequent Cardenas with my family all the time and may consider taking all of my business elsewhere, likely Winco.

After that conversation I decided to leave my shopping cart where it was and walked out. I called the store and spoke to a supervisor by the name of Manuela, she reaffirmed their stance on videos or photography. I understand that every business has a right to their own policies but I couldn't disagree more with it. So many businesses have those "people love us on Yelp" stickers and rely heavily on word of mouth. So many places that I have found and now frequent are because of yelp, because of customer reviews, and of course, those amazing pictures that people post.</Text><Pics>None<//Pics><Response>None< /Response><GmapID>0x80c34c7996146f63:0x6d78d76fff05b1f5</GmapID></record></dataset><record>
